	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Pan American Games</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan-American_Games&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan-American Games">Pan-American Games</a>)</span></div>

<p>The <b>Pan American Games</b> (also known colloquially as the <b>Pan Am Games</b>) is a major sporting event in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> featuring summer sports, in which thousands of athletes participate in a <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">variety of competitions</a>. The competition is held among athletes from nations of the Americas, every four years in the year before the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a>. The only <a href="/wiki/1990_Winter_Pan_American_Games" title="1990 Winter Pan American Games">Winter Pan American Games were held in 1990</a>. In 2021, there will be a <a href="/wiki/2021_Junior_Pan_American_Games" title="2021 Junior Pan American Games">Junior Pan American Games</a> for young athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-radiocentrodeportesjunoir_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radiocentrodeportesjunoir-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mexicannocjunior_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mexicannocjunior-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lavanguardiajuniors_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lavanguardiajuniors-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-panamjuniorsodepa_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panamjuniorsodepa-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Sports_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American Sports Organization">Pan American Sports Organization</a> (PASO) is the governing body of the Pan American Games movement, whose structure and actions are defined by the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Charter" title="Olympic Charter">Olympic Charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-para_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-para-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2019_Pan_American_Games" title="2019 Pan American Games">XVIII Pan American Games</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a> from July 26–August 11; the <a href="/wiki/2023_Pan_American_Games" title="2023 Pan American Games">XIX Pan American Games</a> will be held in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a> between 20 October-5 November. Since the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">XV Pan American Games in 2007</a> , host cities are contracted to manage both the Pan American and the <a href="/wiki/Parapan_American_Games" title="Parapan American Games">Parapan American Games</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-para_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-para-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> in which athletes with physical disabilities compete with one another. The Parapan American Games are held immediately following the Pan American Games.
</p><p>The Pan American Games Movement consists of <a href="/wiki/List_of_international_sport_federations" class="mw-redirect" title="List of international sport federations">international sports federations</a> (IFs), <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> (NOCs) that are recognized by PASO, and organizing committees for each specific Pan American Games. As the decision-making body, PASO is responsible for choosing the host city for each Pan American Games. The host city is responsible for organizing and funding a celebration of the Games consistent with the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Charter" title="Olympic Charter">Olympic Charter</a> (since PASO is affiliated with the IOC, the Olympic Charter) and rules. The Pan American Games program, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games_sports" title="Pan American Games sports">sports</a> to be contested at the Games, is determined by PASO. The celebration of the Games encompasses many rituals and symbols, such as the flag and torch, and the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games_ceremony" title="Olympic Games ceremony">opening and closing ceremonies</a>. Over 5,000 athletes compete at the Pan American Games in 36 sports and nearly 400 events. The first, second, and third-place finishers in each event receive gold, silver, and bronze medals, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_games">Early games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The idea of holding a Pan American Games was first raised at the <a href="/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics" title="1932 Summer Olympics">1932 Summer Olympics</a> in Los Angeles, where Latin American representatives of the International Olympic Committee (IOC) suggested that a competition among all the countries in the Americas should be created.<sup id="cite_ref-first_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The first event called the Pan American Games took place in <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a> in 1937 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Texas_%26_Pan-American_Exposition" title="Greater Texas &amp; Pan-American Exposition">Greater Texas &amp; Pan-American Exposition</a>, but it attracted so little attention it has never counted in the records of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the first Pan American Sports Congress, held in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> in 1940, the participants decided that the first games should be held in Buenos Aires in 1942. The plans had to be postponed because of World War II. A second Pan American Sports Congress held in London during the <a href="/wiki/1948_Summer_Olympics" title="1948 Summer Olympics">1948 Summer Olympics</a> reconfirmed Buenos Aires as the choice of host city for the inaugural games, which were <a href="/wiki/1951_Pan_American_Games" title="1951 Pan American Games">held in 1951</a>. The games offered 18 sports.<sup id="cite_ref-first_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Countries that were part of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> such as Canada did not compete at the first Pan American Games.<sup id="cite_ref-canhist_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canhist-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The second games were held in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. Competitions started on March 12 and included 2,583 athletes from 22 countries, competing in 17 sports.<sup id="cite_ref-u_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-u-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Pan American Games have been held subsequently every four years.<sup id="cite_ref-u_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-u-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_games">Recent games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recent games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg/200px-Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg/300px-Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg/400px-Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Village_Welcome_Centre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The welcome centre at the 2015 Pan American Games athletes' village.</div></div></div>
<p>While the inaugural 1951 Games hosted 2,513 participants representing 14 nations, the most recent <a href="/wiki/2015_Pan_American_Games" title="2015 Pan American Games">2015 Pan American Games</a> involved 6,132 competitors from 41 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-first_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> During the games most athletes and officials are housed in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Village" title="Olympic Village">Pan American Games village</a>. This village is intended to be a self-contained home for all the participants. It is furnished with cafeterias, health clinics, and locations for religious expression.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>PASO allows nations to compete that do not meet the strict requirements for political sovereignty that other international organizations demand. As a result, colonies and dependencies are permitted to set up their own National Olympic Committees. Examples of this include territories such as <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> which compete as separate nations despite being legally under the jurisdiction of another power.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Winter_Pan_American_Games">Winter Pan American Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Winter Pan American Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1990_Winter_Pan_American_Games" title="1990 Winter Pan American Games">1990 Winter Pan American Games</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg/220px-Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg/330px-Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg/440px-Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Le%C3%B1as_Mendoza_Argentina_by_Andre_Charland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Las_Le%C3%B1as" title="Las Leñas">Las Leñas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, hosted the only Pan American Winter Games.</div></div></div>
<p>There have been attempts to hold Winter Pan American Games throughout the history of the games, but these have had little success.<sup id="cite_ref-ioc_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> An initial attempt to hold winter events was made by the organizers of the 1951 Pan American Games in Buenos Aires, who planned to stage winter events later in the year but dropped the idea due to lack of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-EB-history_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-history-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
Reliable winter snow in the Americas is limited to two countries, the United States and Canada. Andean winter weather is often fickle, and higher elevation areas in South America with annual snow often lack the infrastructure to host major sporting events. Another difficulty is that the Americas cover two hemispheres, which creates scheduling issues related to reverse seasons.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Lake_Placid,_New_York" title="Lake Placid, New York">Lake Placid, New York</a> tried to organize Winter Games in 1959 but, again, not enough countries expressed interest. The plans were eventually cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-ioc_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1988, members of PASO voted to hold the first Pan American Winter Games at <a href="/wiki/Las_Le%C3%B1as" title="Las Leñas">Las Leñas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> in September 1989. It was further agreed that Winter Games would be held every four years. Lack of snow however, forced the postponement of the games until September 16–22, 1990<sup id="cite_ref-ioc_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> when only eight countries sent 97 athletes to Las Leñas. Of that total, 76 were from just three countries: Argentina, Canada, and the United States. Weather was unseasonably warm and again there was little snow, so only three Alpine Skiing events&#160;– the Slalom, Giant Slalom, and Super G were staged. The United States and Canada won all 18 medals.
</p><p>PASO awarded the second Pan American Winter Games to <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> for 1993. The United States warned that it would not take part unless a full schedule of events was held. The Santiago organizing committee eventually gave up on planning the Games after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Olympic_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Olympic Committee">United States Olympic Committee</a> declined to participate, and the idea has not been revived since.<sup id="cite_ref-ioc_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_Pan_American_Games">Junior Pan American Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Junior Pan American Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2021_Junior_Pan_American_Games" title="2021 Junior Pan American Games">2021 Junior Pan American Games</a></div>
<p>On January 16, 2019 PASO announced the creation of the Junior Pan American Games. This event, inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Youth_Olympic_Games" title="Youth Olympic Games">Youth Olympic Games</a>, is exclusive for athletes who are under 21 years of age, with less requirements on infrastructure and cost.<sup id="cite_ref-panamjuniorsodepa_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panamjuniorsodepa-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mexicannocjunior_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mexicannocjunior-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-radiocentrodeportesjunoir_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radiocentrodeportesjunoir-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the <a href="/wiki/2021_Junior_Pan_American_Games" title="2021 Junior Pan American Games">first edition of the games</a>, Panam Sports accepted candidate cities until January 31. <a href="/wiki/Cali,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cali, Colombia">Cali, Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana,_El_Salvador" title="Santa Ana, El Salvador">Santa Ana, El Salvador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monterrey,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Monterrey, Mexico">Monterrey, Mexico</a> were accepted as candidate cities.<sup id="cite_ref-ATR_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATR-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Cali, Colombia was chosen as the host city at the Executive Committee in <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9,_Costa_Rica" title="San José, Costa Rica">San José, Costa Rica</a> on March 27, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pan_American_Sports_Organization">Pan American Sports Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pan American Sports Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Panam_Sports" title="Panam Sports">Panam Sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Sports_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American Sports Organization">Pan American Sports Organization</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pwowo.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Pwowo.PNG/220px-Pwowo.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Pwowo.PNG/330px-Pwowo.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Pwowo.PNG/440px-Pwowo.PNG 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pwowo.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/2015_Pan_American_Games_opening_ceremony" title="2015 Pan American Games opening ceremony">2015 Pan American Games opening ceremony</a> had announcements in English, Spanish and French.</div></div></div>
<p>The Pan American Games Movement encompasses a number of national and international sporting organizations and federations, recognized media partners, athletes, officials, judges, and every other person and institution that agrees to abide by the rules of the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Charter" title="Olympic Charter">Olympic Charter</a> (which is the same as PASO's charter).<sup id="cite_ref-movement_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-movement-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> As the umbrella organization of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">Olympic Movement</a>, PASO is responsible for selecting the host city, overseeing the planning of the Pan American Games, updating and approving the sports program, and negotiating sponsorship and broadcasting rights.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Pan American Games Movement is made of three major elements:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_international_sport_federations" class="mw-redirect" title="List of international sport federations">International Federations</a> (IFs) are the <a href="/wiki/Sport_governing_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport governing body">governing bodies</a> that supervise a sport at an international level. For example, the International Federation of Association Football (<a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>) is the IF for <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football (soccer)</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_Volleyball" title="Fédération Internationale de Volleyball">Fédération Internationale de Volleyball</a> (FIVB) is the international governing body for <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>. There are currently 36 IFs in the Pan American Games Movement, representing each of the Pan American Games sports.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> (NOCs) represent and regulate the Pan American Games movement within each country. For example, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Olympic_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Olympic Committee">United States Olympic Committee</a> (USOC) is the NOC of the United States. There are currently 42 NOCs recognized by PASO.</li>
<li>Organizing Committees for the Pan America Games (PAOGs) constitute the temporary committees responsible for the organization of a specific celebration of the Pan American Games. PAOGs are dissolved after each Games, once the final report is delivered to PASO.</li></ul>
<p>Spanish and English are the official languages of the Pan American Games Movement. The other language used at each Pan American Games is the language of the host country. For example: at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">2007 Pan American Games</a> who was held in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, the first language was <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Brazilian Portuguese</a>.  Every proclamation (such as the announcement of each country during the parade of nations in the opening ceremony) is spoken in these three languages or the main two depending on whether the host country is an English or Spanish speaking country.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg/220px-Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg/330px-Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg/440px-Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2772" data-file-height="1866" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pan_Flame_Rio_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Pan American Games torch being lit in <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a>.</div></div></div>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small-left noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;float:left">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:PASO_Hymn.ogg" title="File:PASO Hymn.ogg">The Anthem of PASO</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="14" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="PASO_Hymn.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c1/PASO_Hymn.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (50 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="49677" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/c/c1/PASO_Hymn.ogg/PASO_Hymn.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="138064" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Adopted in 2008</div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>The Pan American Games Movement uses symbols to represent the ideals embodied in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Charter" title="Olympic Charter">Pan American Games charter</a>. The Pan American Sports Organization flag displays the PASO logo on a white background. To highlight the close association between the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> and the Pan Am Games, the Olympic Rings were added to the flag in 1988. The flag has been hoisted during each celebration of the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-flag_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flag-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The flag was hoisted while the Olympic Hymn was played until the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">2007 Games</a>. In 2011 Games, the new anthem was played for the first time. The anthem itself was composed in 2008.
</p><p>Similar to the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_flame" title="Olympic flame">Olympic flame</a>, the Pan American Games flame is lit well before the Games are to commence. The flame was lit for the first games in <a href="/wiki/Olympia,_Greece" title="Olympia, Greece">Olympia, Greece</a>. For subsequent games, the torch has been lit by <a href="/wiki/Aztec" class="mw-redirect" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> people in ancient temples, first in the <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_la_Estrella_National_Park" title="Cerro de la Estrella National Park">Cerro de la Estrella</a> and later in the <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_the_Sun" title="Pyramid of the Sun">Pyramid of the Sun</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a> Pyramids.<sup id="cite_ref-torch_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torch-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The only exception was for the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> games in 1963, when the torch was lit in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a> by the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaraní people</a>. An Aztec then lights the torch of the first relay bearer, thus initiating the Pan American Games torch relay that will carry the flame to the host city's main stadium, where it plays an important role in the opening ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Since 2011, the flame is required to be held during the games in the stadium which will host the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a> competition. If the Opening ceremony and athletics competition will be held in different stadiums, the flame will be required to move from one stadium to the other. Exceptions occurred in the <a href="/wiki/1987_Pan_American_Games" title="1987 Pan American Games">1987</a>, <a href="/wiki/1999_Pan_American_Games" title="1999 Pan American Games">1999</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">2007 Games</a>, each of which had only one cauldron.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Pan American Games <a href="/wiki/Sports_mascot" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports mascot">mascot</a>, an animal or human figure representing the cultural heritage of the host country, was introduced in <a href="/wiki/1979_Pan_American_Games" title="1979 Pan American Games">1979</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> It has played an important part on the Games identity and promotion. The mascot of the most recent Pan American Games, in <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>, was Milco, a inca statue.
</p><p>List of Games mascots:<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>San Juan 1979: Coqui (frog)</li>
<li>Caracas 1983: Santiaguito (lion)</li>
<li>Indianapolis 1987: Amigo (green parrot)</li>
<li>Havana 1991: Tocopan (bird)</li>
<li>Mar del Plata 1995: Lobi (sea lion)</li>
<li>Winnipeg 1999: Duck and Lorita (ducks)</li>
<li>Santo Domingo 2003: Tito (manatee)</li>
<li>Rio de Janeiro 2007: Cauê (sun)</li>
<li>Guadalajara 2011: Huichi (deer), Gavo (agave plant) and Leo (lion)</li>
<li>Toronto 2015: Pachi (porcupine)</li>
<li>Lima 2019: Milco (statue)<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceremonies">Ceremonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ceremonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games_ceremony" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American Games ceremony">Pan American Games ceremony</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening">Opening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Opening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firelinepanam.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Firelinepanam.PNG/200px-Firelinepanam.PNG" decoding="async" width="200" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Firelinepanam.PNG/300px-Firelinepanam.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Firelinepanam.PNG/400px-Firelinepanam.PNG 2x" data-file-width="749" data-file-height="411" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firelinepanam.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A scene from the opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Pan_American_Games" title="2015 Pan American Games">2015 Pan American Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a></div></div></div>
<p>As mandated by the Olympic Charter, various elements frame the opening ceremony of the Pan American Games.<sup id="cite_ref-OCFactSheetS_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCFactSheetS-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The ceremony typically starts with the hoisting of the host country's flag and a performance of its national anthem.<sup id="cite_ref-OCFactSheetS_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCFactSheetS-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The host nation then presents artistic displays of music, singing, dance, and theater representative of its culture and history.<sup id="cite_ref-OCFactSheetS_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCFactSheetS-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The artistic presentations have grown in scale and complexity as successive hosts attempt to provide a ceremony that outlasts its predecessor's in terms of memorability. The opening ceremony of the Guadalajara Games reportedly cost $20&#160;million, with much of the cost incurred in the artistic segment.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the artistic portion of the ceremony, the athletes parade into the stadium grouped by nation. Argentina is traditionally the first nation to enter in order to honor the origins of the Pan American Games, similar to how Greece enters first in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> as the originator. Nations usually then enter the stadium alphabetically according to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish language</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/1995_Pan_American_Games" title="1995 Pan American Games">1995 Pan American Games</a>, which was hosted in <a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">Mar del Plata</a>, Argentina, the Argentine flag entered the stadium first, while the country's delegation entered last (similar to what happened with Greece in the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a>). Speeches are given, formally opening the Games. Finally, the Pan American Games torch is brought into the stadium and passed on until it reaches the final torch carrier—often a well-known and successful athlete from the host nation—who lights the Pan American Games flame in the stadium's cauldron.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Closing">Closing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Closing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg/200px-Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg/300px-Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg/400px-Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2780" data-file-height="1840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2007_closing_ceremony_6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Athletes gather in the stadium during the closing ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">2007 Pan American Games</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The closing ceremony of the Pan American Games takes place after all sporting events have concluded. Flag-bearers from each participating country enter the stadium, followed by the athletes who enter together, without any national distinction.
</p><p>Two national flags along with the flag of PASO are hoisted while the corresponding national anthems are played: the flag of the current host country and the flag of the country hosting the next Pan American Games.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The president of the organizing committee and the president of PASO make their closing speeches, the Games are officially closed, and the Pan American Games family is invited to participate at the next Games. The Pan American flame is then extinguished.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In what is known as the Antwerp Ceremony, the mayor of the city that organized the Games transfers a special Pan American Games flag to the president of PASO, who then passes it on to the mayor of the city hosting the next Games.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> After these compulsory elements, the next host nation briefly introduces itself with artistic displays of dance and theater representative of its culture. The closing ceremony includes a fifteen-minute presentation from the next host city.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medal_presentation">Medal presentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Medal presentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG/200px-1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG/300px-1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG/400px-1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="1890" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1987_Pan_American_Games_-_U.S._trap_shooting_team.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A medal ceremony during the <a href="/wiki/1987_Pan_American_Games" title="1987 Pan American Games">1987 Pan American Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>At the conclusion of each event, medals are ceremoniously distributed to the first, second and third-place finishers. The participants stand a three-tiered podium while receiving their medals.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> After the medals are given out by an IOC or PASO member, the national flags of the three medalists are raised while the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of the gold medalist's country plays.<sup id="cite_ref-otraditions_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otraditions-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Volunteering citizens of the host country act as hosts during the medal ceremonies, as they aid the officials who present the medals and act as flag-bearers.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> For every Pan American Games event, the respective medal ceremony is held, at most, one day after the event's final. When athletics was scheduled for the last days, the men's marathon is held in the last day of the games, and the award ceremony is held before or during the closing ceremonies.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games_sports" title="Pan American Games sports">Pan American Games sports</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions_and_medalists">Champions and medalists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Champions and medalists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Pan_American_Games_medalists" title="Category:Pan American Games medalists">Category:Pan American Games medalists</a> and <a href="/wiki/All-time_Pan_American_Games_medal_table" title="All-time Pan American Games medal table">All-time Pan American Games medal table</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg/200px-Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg/300px-Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg/400px-Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2224" data-file-height="3096" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thiago_Pereira_Gold_Pan_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Swimmer <a href="/wiki/Thiago_Pereira" title="Thiago Pereira">Thiago Pereira</a> of Brazil has a record 23 Pan American medals.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Here he holds a gold medal during the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">2007 edition</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The athletes or teams who place first, second, or third in each event receive medals. The winners receive gold medals, while the runners-up receive silver medals and the third-place athletes are awarded bronze medals. In events contested by a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">single-elimination tournament</a> (most notably boxing), third place might not be determined and both semifinal losers receive bronze medals. PASO does not keep statistics of medals won, but National Olympic Committees and the media record medal statistics as a measure of success.
</p><p>The top ten nations all time at the Pan American Games (minus medals won at the Winter Pan American Games):<sup id="cite_ref-medal_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medal-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li>Record <br /> Summer Pan American Games 1995 <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" />&#160;</span>United States, 424 medals</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Pan_American_Games">List of Pan American Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: List of Pan American Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png/300px-Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png/450px-Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png/600px-Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1938" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pan_American_Games_host_countries.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Pan American Games locations (host cities in red dots). Countries that have hosted one Pan Am Games are shaded green, while countries that have hosted two or more are shaded blue.</div></div></div>
<p>The host city for a Pan American Games is usually chosen six years ahead of their celebration. The process of selection is carried out in two phases that span a two-year period. The prospective host city applies to its country's Olympic Committee; if more than one city from the same country submits a proposal to its NOC, the national committee typically holds an internal selection, since only one city per NOC can be presented to the Pan American Sports Organization for consideration. Once the deadline for submission of proposals by the NOCs is reached, the first phase (Application) begins with the applicant cities asked to complete a questionnaire regarding several key criteria related to the organization of the Pan American Games Games.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In this form, the applicants must give assurances that they will comply with the Olympic Charter and with any other regulations established by PASO's Executive Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The evaluation of the filled questionnaires by a specialized group provides PASO with an overview of each applicant's project and their potential to host the Games. On the basis of this technical evaluation, PASO's Executive Board selects the applicants that will proceed to the candidature stage.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Once the candidate cities are selected, they must submit to PASO a bigger and more detailed presentation of their project as part of a candidature file. Each city is thoroughly analyzed by an evaluation commission. This commission will visit the candidate cities, interviewing local officials and inspecting prospective venue sites, and submit a report on its findings one month before the PASO's final decision. During the interview process the candidate city must guarantee that it will be able to fund the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> After the work of the evaluation commission, a list of candidates is presented to the General Session of PASO, which is assembled in a country that must not have a candidate city in the running. The members of PASO gathered in the Session have the final vote on the host city. Once elected, the host city bid committee (together with the NOC of the respective country) signs a Host City Contract with PASO, officially becoming a Pan American Games host nation and host city.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_6-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Pan American Games have been hosted by 16 cities in 11 countries. Mexico and Canada have hosted three Pan American Games each, more than any other nation. Among cities, only <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">Winnipeg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> have played host to the Pan American Games more than once, each hosting twice.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_nations">Participating nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan_American_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Participating nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All 41 countries whose <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committee</a> is recognized by the Pan American Sports Organization compete at the Pan American Games.<sup id="cite_ref-nations_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nations-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
